## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed three local rows present as three sources when a diff run this session proves rows two and three byte-identical, the unclassified-yet copy duplicates the idiomatic-references file exactly, so the theme's evidence base is one router plus one standalone merge, not three documents
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the corpus inherited files from multiple archive sweeps and the unclassified folder holds material awaiting classification, duplication across sweeps is a filing artifact, not independent corroboration
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: counting the duplicate as corroboration inflates confidence, two identical files agreeing is one author speaking twice, and any future divergence between the copies would signal an edit event, not a disagreement between sources
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: provenance for this document's statements, the four external URLs stayed unretrieved throughout this evolution and confer no current-fact authority
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to annotate the mapping with the deduplication finding, cite the idiomatic-references path as the canonical copy, and treat the unclassified path as a filing duplicate pending its classification

## Section 012: Local Corpus Hierarchy
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed file-position roles miss the actual precedence structure, the router is canonical for dispatch and reading order, the merge is canonical for nothing, every doctrine section it carries is a compression of some sibling or bundle theme, and the duplicate copy carries no authority at all beyond confirming the merge circulated
- **supporting_reason:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the merge declares itself a merger of the bundle's strongest parts, so by its own charter it is derivative, authoritative only in contexts where its sources are unreachable, a situational authority rather than a structural one
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: settling doctrine disputes from the merge when routed sources are reachable resolves them from compressions, the requirement template stripped of the playbook's process, the anti-pattern list stripped of repair clauses
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: precedence among this theme's three mapped files and their relation to the bundle, cross-corpus precedence belongs to adjacent routing
- **revision_decision:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to record the working hierarchy, router canonical for navigation, routed siblings and their evolved themes canonical for doctrine, merge authoritative only when detached, duplicate authoritative never
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that situational authority is this hierarchy's exportable idea, a document can be the right authority in one context and the wrong one in another without any edit, the merge's authority is a function of what else the reader can reach, not of its content
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to resolve navigation questions from the router, doctrine questions from the deepest reachable source, and cite the merge as authority only alongside a statement that nothing deeper was reachable
- **supporting_reason:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the merge declares itself a merger of the bundle's strongest parts, so by its own charter it is derivative, authoritative only in contexts where its sources are unreachable, a situational authority rather than a structural one

## Section 013: Theme Specific Artifact
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed generic worked-example artifact misses this theme's natural object, a routing manifest for any context that receives bundle material, one block recording which shape was shipped, router or merge, which sibling paths were verified resolvable at shipping time, which canonical copy the merge was taken from, and the date of the reachability check
- **supporting_reason:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because every failure this theme names, dead sibling references, duplicate-counting, silent compression loss, is a packaging-time fact that becomes invisible after shipping, the manifest preserves exactly the facts consumers cannot reconstruct
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: without the manifest, a consumer holding a router with dead paths cannot tell a broken copy from a broken bundle, and a consumer holding a divergent merge copy cannot tell edits from corruption
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: one manifest per shipped bundle context, gate records belong to the gates theme and boundary ledgers to the reliability theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to define the artifact as the routing manifest with four fields, shape shipped, paths verified, canonical source, check date, attached wherever bundle material travels

## Section 014: Worked Example Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed abstract usage lines stand where this theme wants a routing rehearsal, take one concrete request, an async service with a vague success criterion, walk the router, mode classification catches Spec plus Delivery, the task-type order sequences playbook then reliability sections then gates, and contrast the same request answered from the merge alone
- **supporting_reason:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the contrast run teaches the shapes' tradeoff concretely, the routed path surfaces the playbook's full requirement process while the merge path reaches its compressed template immediately, speed against depth made visible on one request
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: engineers who never run the contrast default to whichever shape they met first, router loyalists over-read in portable contexts and merge loyalists under-read in-bundle, both from habit rather than fit
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: teaching this theme's routing decisions, rehearsals of the routed doctrine belong to the owning themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to anchor the section on the contrast rehearsal plus one packaging drill, hand the learner a router with one deliberately broken sibling path and require the manifest check to catch it before any reading starts
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the broken-path drill teaches the theme's least intuitive lesson, navigation artifacts fail silently, a router with a dead reference reads as confidently as a healthy one, and only the resolution check distinguishes them, confidence in a map says nothing about the territory
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed symbol-count boundary misprices this theme's work, whose units are per-consultation routing cost, the fixed small read of the router before any task, per-packaging cost when bundle material ships to a new context with its manifest, and per-audit cost for the count-and-diff cycle including the duplicate re-check
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because routing cost is tiny and constant while its savings scale with the size of the references not loaded, packaging cost is rare and bursty, and audit cost is periodic, so the theme's economics are dominated by how often heavy references would otherwise load unrouted
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: pricing this work per symbol makes the router look like pure overhead, ninety-one lines read before every task, when its value is precisely the hundreds of lines per task it prevents, symbol accounting inverts the theme's value
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: budgeting routing, packaging, and audit work for this theme, the routed content's implementation workload belongs to its own themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to restate the model in three units, fixed routing read per consultation, manifest cost per shipping event, and count-and-diff cost per audit cycle
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the routing read amortizes within a single task, unlike most fixed costs that amortize across tasks, one avoided sibling load repays the router read severalfold immediately, which is why route-first survives even under deadline pressure that strips other disciplines

## Section 019: Reliability Target
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed document-property thresholds stand where routing invariants should, every bundle consultation preceded by a routing decision, every shipped bundle context carrying a current manifest, every corpus citation of the merge naming the canonical path, and every audit cycle re-verifying the duplicate identity with a dated result
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because each target operationalizes one theme mechanism, the consultation target holds the route-first thesis, the manifest target holds packaging discipline, the citation target holds canonicalization, and the re-diff target keeps the theme's one volatile claim measured
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: informally held, these targets decay in the usual order, routing lapses first under deadline, manifests stop refreshing on bundle revisions, and the citation rule erodes as downstream documents copy each other's references
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: routing and packaging invariants for this theme, doctrine-quality targets belong to the routed themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to publish the four targets with evidence methods, consultation sampling for routing, shipped-context audit for manifests, downstream citation review for canonical paths, and the dated re-diff in each audit record
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the re-diff target is the only self-expiring one, the others decay through neglect while this one decays through time alone, every day since the last diff widens the window in which either copy could have changed, so its evidence method needs a maximum age, not just a presence check

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the pairing closes the loop from both ends, no performance requirement without units means every stated threshold is testable, and no performance testing without stated thresholds means every test verifies a real contract, neither vague claims nor aimless benchmarks survive
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: breaking either half re-opens the classic failures, unitless requirements produce unfalsifiable fast-enough claims, and threshold-less benchmarking produces numbers with no contract to violate, measurement theater in both directions
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: how performance claims get specified and triggered for verification under this theme's carriers, benchmark construction lives with the reliability theme's correctness-preserving doctrine

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed task-splitting bounds stand beside this theme's real scale seams, the router's dispatch assumes one bundle with four siblings, the merge assumes one file can still carry the doctrine, and both assumptions break as the corpus grows, more bundles need cross-bundle routing the router never models, and doctrine growth eventually overflows any single-file compression
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because routing artifacts are sized to their corpus generation, the router's four modes and six task types partition the 202604 bundle's space, and each new theme, bundle, or doctrine area added since strains a partition that has no extension mechanism
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: stretched past its seams, the router silently misroutes, new risk categories fall into the nearest old mode, and the merge's compression drops proportionally more as its sources grow, both artifacts degrading without any visible failure event
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: bounding this theme's routing and packaging patterns, the routed doctrine's own scale limits belong to its themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to name the seams with triggers, a second bundle triggers a cross-bundle routing layer above per-bundle routers, doctrine growth past what the merge's shape absorbs triggers regeneration or splitting, and corpus-wide routing belongs to the corpus's own maps, not to any bundle's router

## Section 025: Future Refresh Search Queries
